  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18117164645009685968">In the year 1605 a young woman, hiding from her past, takes up the veil becoming Soeur Auguste. Five years later the past has found her and to protect herself and her beloved child she'll have to perform one last act of dazzling daring more audacious than any she has previously attempted.<br/><br/>With her internationally bestselling novels Chocolat, Blackberry Wine, Five Quarters o</span>
  <span id="freeText18117164645009685968" style="display:none">In the year 1605 a young woman, hiding from her past, takes up the veil becoming Soeur Auguste. Five years later the past has found her and to protect herself and her beloved child she'll have to perform one last act of dazzling daring more audacious than any she has previously attempted.<br /><br />With her internationally bestselling novels Chocolat, Blackberry Wine, Five Quarters of the Orange, and Coastliners, Joanne Harris has woven intoxicating spells that celebrate the sensuous while exposing the passion, secrets and folly beneath the surface of rustic village life. In Holy Fools, her most ambitious and accomplished novel to date, she transports us back to a time of intrigue and turmoil, of deception and masquerade. <br /><br />In the year 1605, a young widow, pregnant and alone, seeks sanctuary at the small Abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-mer on the island of Noirs Moustiers off the Brittany coast. After the birth of her daughter, she takes up the veil, and a new name, Soeur Auguste. But the peace she has found in remote isolation is shattered five years later by the events that follow the death of her kind benefactress, the Reverend Mother. <br /><br />When a new abbess -- the daughter of a corrupt noble family elevated by the murder of King Henri IV -- arrives at Sainte Marie-de-la-mer, she does not arrive alone. With her is her personal confessor and spiritual guide, Père Colombin, a man Soeur Auguste knows all too well. For the newcomer is Guy LeMerle, a charlatan and seducer now masquerading as a priest, and the one man she fears more than any other. <br /><br />Soeur Auguste has a secret. Once she was l'Ailée, "The Winged One," star performer of a troupe led by LeMerle, before betrayal forced her to change her identity. But now the past has found her. Before long, thanks to LeMerle, suspicion and debauchery are breeding like a plague within the convent's walls -- fueled by dark rumors of witchcraft, part of the false priest's brilliantly orchestrated scheme of revenge. To protect herself and her beloved child, l'Ailée will have to perform one last act of dazzling daring more audacious than any she has previously attempted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18117164645009685968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Edgarr Alien Pooh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111745799-edgarr-alien-pooh"><img alt="Edgarr Alien Pooh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585112748p2/111745799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3552274869?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edgarr Alien Pooh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edgarr Alien Pooh" href="/user/show/111745799-edgarr-alien-pooh">Edgarr Alien Pooh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385603645" href="/book/show/902747.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111745799-edgarr-alien-pooh?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3552274869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16975535085842671676">I finally read a Joanne Harris book. Have looked at these books for years and have always loved the covers but thought they could be winners or losers for me but this was a winner!<br/><br/>A young lady spends her early years traveling and performing with a gypsy troupe, meeting people along the way who will have great impressions on her life. After several run-ins and close calls, the troupe disbands spreading to various parts of France. <br/><br/>Juliette finds herself in a convent where she lives an easy life wi</span>
  <span id="freeText16975535085842671676" style="display:none">I finally read a Joanne Harris book. Have looked at these books for years and have always loved the covers but thought they could be winners or losers for me but this was a winner!<br /><br />A young lady spends her early years traveling and performing with a gypsy troupe, meeting people along the way who will have great impressions on her life. After several run-ins and close calls, the troupe disbands spreading to various parts of France. <br /><br />Juliette finds herself in a convent where she lives an easy life with a group of Nuns, several from similar backgrounds. But she can't escape her past and eventually, it catches up with her. But things have changed within Juliette through the years and now she will deal with her past. But she is not prepared for what is to come.<br /><br />Again I must say I am not one to read much historical fiction, and this book takes place in the year 1610, but I really delved into this. I enjoy historical non-fiction reads and felt that the research for the times of this story was vast.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book far more than I hoped too. It has a great cast of female characters, a fast moving plot and a fair amount of underhanded dealings. I'm sure to read more of Joanne's books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16975535085842671676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_57775340" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57775340" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/250717-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485363504p2/250717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57775340?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/250717-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060559137" href="/book/show/15146.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57775340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7898008284726669657">I have mixed feelings about this book. It was a nice contrast and complement after <u>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5043.The_Pillars_of_the_Earth' title='The Pillars of the Earth by Ken Follett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pillars of the Earth</a>
</u>, as that book was set in a monastery in England and this one in a convent in France, though 500 years later. I have not read <u>Chocolat</u> by Harris, but of course I have seen the movie and thoroughly enjoyed it.<br/><br/>This book is quite different—much darker and without a satisfactory ending (in my opinion). I liked the character development of Juliette and the fact that she found peace and comun</span>
  <span id="freeText7898008284726669657" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book. It was a nice contrast and complement after <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5043.The_Pillars_of_the_Earth" title="The Pillars of the Earth by Ken Follett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pillars of the Earth</a>
</u>, as that book was set in a monastery in England and this one in a convent in France, though 500 years later. I have not read <u>Chocolat</u> by Harris, but of course I have seen the movie and thoroughly enjoyed it.<br /><br />This book is quite different—much darker and without a satisfactory ending (in my opinion). I liked the character development of Juliette and the fact that she found peace and comunity at the island convent after her rather troubled past as a gypsy and circus performer. She sought refuge there after she realized she was pregnant, and for awhile she is able to lead a fairly restful life, raising her daughter, tending the herb garden, and teaching Latin to the novices. This all changes when LeMerle, a man from her past, arrives masquerading as a priest with the new strict abbess, with his own evil agenda.<br /> <br />One of the most interesting tidbits of the book was that while the sculpture of the patron saint of the convent, Maire-de-la-mer, is said to be the Holy Mother, it is more than likely a mermaid. While another reviewer has pointed out that this church does not in fact exist, it made me think again how the pagan customs of local people were often merged into the Catholic belief system. It was akin to the blood oath at the Scottish marriage in <u>Outlander</u> by Gabaldon, as well as the Celtic practice that married monks were acceptable in Ireland long after such practices were banned elsewhere, as mentioned in Rutherford’s <u>The Princes of Ireland</u>. This blending of the pagan and the holy pervades the book, manifested not just in the sculpture, but also in Juliette’s herbal remedies as well as her surreptitious card readings to divine LeMerle’s purpose at the convent. <br /><br />The mystery/thriller aspect of the book did keep me riveted, and I finished it in a few hours this afternoon by the pool. However, I felt the ending would have been better if Harris had finished after the final scene at the convent. Overall, I would recommend it as escapist summer reading, with a darker overtone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7898008284726669657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82216777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82216777" />
    <a title="Ana Mardoll" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3078990-ana-mardoll"><img alt="Ana Mardoll" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519954099p2/3078990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82216777?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana Mardoll" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana Mardoll" href="/user/show/3078990-ana-mardoll">Ana Mardoll</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552770019" href="/book/show/1022698.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3078990-ana-mardoll?shelf=ana-reviewed">ana-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82216777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6972714437278713001">Holy Fools / 0-552-77001-9<br/><br/>What happened here? I loved "Chocolat", and I adored "Five Quarters of the Orange". "Holy Fools", however, seems like it came from a completely different author. The book is acceptable, but not up to Harris' standards. <br/><br/>To start, the Mother-Daughter theme that Harris employs so well is deeply underdeveloped here as more of a plot device than anything else. There was a lot of potential here: a nun with a beloved daughter, raising her to be safe from the outside world and </span>
  <span id="freeText6972714437278713001" style="display:none">Holy Fools / 0-552-77001-9<br /><br />What happened here? I loved "Chocolat", and I adored "Five Quarters of the Orange". "Holy Fools", however, seems like it came from a completely different author. The book is acceptable, but not up to Harris' standards. <br /><br />To start, the Mother-Daughter theme that Harris employs so well is deeply underdeveloped here as more of a plot device than anything else. There was a lot of potential here: a nun with a beloved daughter, raising her to be safe from the outside world and yet perhaps a little too sheltered. Unfortunately, the daughter seems a little underdeveloped - neither rebellious and wanting to know the curiosities of the outside world nor a little too content in her cocoon. Instead, the daughter seems only to exist to serve as a kidnap/hostage victim so that our heroine cannot effectively flee or intervene when the madness begins. <br /><br />I could accept the "daughter as hostage" plot device, were the main character not so otherwise one-dimensional. The evil mustache-twirling villain has abused her in numerous ways, and yet she seems intently less interested in bearing a grudge and more intent on mooning her way back into his bed. Once there, however, it never seems to occur to our heroine to tie him up and "persuade" him to tell her the secret location of her kidnapped daughter; instead, she just focuses on having a nice tumble and heading off cheerily the next morning. The lackluster narrative conflicts deeply with the established character of the narrator - she's been shown to have great survival skills and would manage easily on her own with the child outside the nunnery, so why does it not even occur to her to take a runner? <br /><br />Harris' crisp insight into females isn't just lost on our heroine. All the women in this novel are almost irredeemable idiots. The nuns descend almost instantly into madness under the manipulation of the villain. This isn't presented as religious hysteria; the women seem either intensely stupid or completely eager to join the villain for their own selfish reasons. The subtlety necessary for religious hysteria seems completely absent here, which is astonishing because I believe that if anyone could have pulled it off, Harris could have. Again, what happened here? <br /><br />This isn't a bad novel. It's got enough cliches to shake a stick at, and it's incredibly frustrating at bits, but so are many decent novels. But this *is* a bad novel for Harris. You may enjoy this, if you check it out at a library, but don't expect Harris quality. In the end, I didn't hate it, but I was deeply disappointed.<br /><br />~ Ana Mardoll</span>
  <a data-text-id="6972714437278713001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_393882754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393882754" />
    <a title="Nimue Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6091697-nimue-brown"><img alt="Nimue Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442613846p2/6091697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393882754?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nimue Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nimue Brown" href="/user/show/6091697-nimue-brown">Nimue Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393882754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8559907568305731313">A gorgeous, compelling story set in mediaeval France, Holy Fools has all the ingredients I love in Joanne Harris’s books. There’s a strong, complex heroine with pagan inclinations, a few villains, a slightly gothic setting, and a lot of less than comfortable reflections on the human condition. Harris has a very warts and all approach to portraying people. She doesn’t tend to do clear lines between the wholly good and the wholly bad, and I love this about her work.<br/><br/>One of the themes running throug</span>
  <span id="freeText8559907568305731313" style="display:none">A gorgeous, compelling story set in mediaeval France, Holy Fools has all the ingredients I love in Joanne Harris’s books. There’s a strong, complex heroine with pagan inclinations, a few villains, a slightly gothic setting, and a lot of less than comfortable reflections on the human condition. Harris has a very warts and all approach to portraying people. She doesn’t tend to do clear lines between the wholly good and the wholly bad, and I love this about her work.<br /><br />One of the themes running through this novel is that way in which people are often complicit in their own oppression. In trying to please the oppressor, and trying to avoid punishment, we give other names to the witch hunter. We accuse someone else to take attention from ourselves. So often what is called for in oppressive scenarios is a banding together to fight off the tyrant. If there’s one tyrant and many people being mistreated, weight of numbers should fix it, but often it doesn’t. Instead, in trying to protect ourselves, we uphold evil systems and support those who abuse us.<br /><br />This is a powerful story, the characters are many and brought to life with consummate skill. I am absolutely convinced that just reading Joanne Harris has the effect of making me a better author. I learn so much from her work, and am constantly aware that I have a lot of learning to do yet.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8559907568305731313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_173197447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173197447" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5524769-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433884193p2/5524769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173197447?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/5524769-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173197447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17971966737910813134">Although I really enjoy reading Harris’s works, I’m beginning to wonder if she has something against the Catholic church. In the majority of the books I’ve read written by her, someone or something from the Catholic church ends up being the baddie, and the Church itself is inevitably portrayed as corrupted and judgmental. I’m not Catholic, but I’d hope that someone who is as lovely an author as she is could branch out a little in her pool for villains.<br/>This book, while still engaging in much magi</span>
  <span id="freeText17971966737910813134" style="display:none">Although I really enjoy reading Harris’s works, I’m beginning to wonder if she has something against the Catholic church. In the majority of the books I’ve read written by her, someone or something from the Catholic church ends up being the baddie, and the Church itself is inevitably portrayed as corrupted and judgmental. I’m not Catholic, but I’d hope that someone who is as lovely an author as she is could branch out a little in her pool for villains.<br />This book, while still engaging in much magical realism, isn’t quite as engaging as some of her other works. It tells the story of Juliette – a former wire walker (a type of acrobatic tight-rope walker) who has abandoned her old life in order to take care of her daughter. She has chosen an out-of-the-way monastery by the ocean in order to do this and has reinvented herself as Sister Auguste. When her past comes back to haunt her in the form of a man she once loved, Juliette must use all her wits and courage in order to save her daughter and the nuns she has come to care for.<br />For some reason, I couldn’t precisely enjoy this story as much as any of Harris’s others. Juliette was interesting, and the suspense built throughout the book was extraordinary…but I never felt quite confident in what was going on. It was as if I never felt in step with the characters. They were there on the page for me to get to know, but I wasn’t interested in them. The story was great, and the setting, and the characters, but it just lacked the zip to hold my interest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17971966737910813134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorottya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorottya" href="/user/show/15478679-dorottya">Dorottya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385603645" href="/book/show/902747.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15478679-dorottya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2157961264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5036411597235413351">Not at all what I anticipated (from the blurb I have read online, I was expecting it to be more of a theatre based story), but I loved it either way.<br/><br/>I loved all the twists and turns in the story, and the fact I could never be sure what to think about each character other than Juliette, our main narrator, because everything that seemed to be true was uncovered to be false... especially behaviours of certain people.<br/><br/>What the novel said about sin, behaviours of people who are not void of sins, what </span>
  <span id="freeText5036411597235413351" style="display:none">Not at all what I anticipated (from the blurb I have read online, I was expecting it to be more of a theatre based story), but I loved it either way.<br /><br />I loved all the twists and turns in the story, and the fact I could never be sure what to think about each character other than Juliette, our main narrator, because everything that seemed to be true was uncovered to be false... especially behaviours of certain people.<br /><br />What the novel said about sin, behaviours of people who are not void of sins, what we choose to believe in, about motherhood and motherly instincts, jealousy etc. was so deeply rooted in real psychology, thus it hit hard for me because of its genuinity. To be honest, I see certain behavioural patterns portrayed in the book more present in today's era THAN EVER. Getting petty revenge on people who ridicule us. Believing in and giving their trust to the people who are cunning and who can sell themselves (if they are attractive, it does not hurt, right?). Using gullible and/or young and inexperienced people to reach one's goal. Suspecting the "weird" people when something is going wrong. People seemingly getting along nicely playing each other out to be near the fire.<br />(not to even talk about how eerily the "theatre part" is resonating with the big abuse scandal of Hollywood... you would have thought we have reached a point where actresses are not treated as prostitutes to prominent men...)<br /><br />But I also liked how religious communities in good times were shown. I do think this was drawn from reality, too - how they sometimes act as refuge for those whose lives seem irrepairable.<br /><br />I liked how the villain was villanous and someone who love to hate with this enigmatic evilness in him - but at the same time, he was not an empty shell, and he had the motivation and a background that can explain his behaviour partly... and also, he was not without emotions. I also loved how our main heroine was not perfectly good, but likeable. I don't have children, but I think I can understand her decisions in th light of her wanting to save her daughter, for which goal she is ready to commit sins. And I also think I understood the dynamics of her relatinship with LeMerle. I can imagine that there is that sort of (partly emotional, partly sexual) passion/attraction that is really hard to break even though you know the other person is only going to cause you misery.<br /><br />Plus... yes, the theatre parts were a huge plus for me as someone whose biggest passion in life is theatre... or at least one of the bigger passions. I really felt there was great research behind those elements.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5036411597235413351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145547557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145547557" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956252-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301595912p2/1956252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145547557?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/1956252-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060559137" href="/book/show/15146.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=catholicism">catholicism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=17th-century">17th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=france">france</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145547557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10890676567437178764">Joanne Harris can spin a tale! I was totally captivated by this magical, medieval story that follows two adversaries who both love and vie with each other. Juliette is a high-wire artist who was raised as a gypsy. She seeks refuge at the Abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-mer when she becomes pregnant with her baby Fleur. She enjoys the quiet life there, tending her herbs, etc., until she once again comes in contact with the Blackbird, the conniving and cruel, yet charming Guy LeMerle, who shows up dis</span>
  <span id="freeText10890676567437178764" style="display:none">Joanne Harris can spin a tale! I was totally captivated by this magical, medieval story that follows two adversaries who both love and vie with each other. Juliette is a high-wire artist who was raised as a gypsy. She seeks refuge at the Abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-mer when she becomes pregnant with her baby Fleur. She enjoys the quiet life there, tending her herbs, etc., until she once again comes in contact with the Blackbird, the conniving and cruel, yet charming Guy LeMerle, who shows up disguised as Père Colombin de Saint-Amand, confessor to the newly appointed abbess. <br /><br />Juliette and LeMerle have been both lovers and antagonists and their relationship is the central theme of Harris’ story. They are like magnets, the positive and negative aspects of their personalities pulling them together and thrusting them apart as they battle each other while at the same time respecting the other’s moves.<br /><br />Set in 17th century France when internal conflicts beset the Catholic church, the story is both theatrical and intense. Harris keeps the reader’s attention with the developing intrigue between her two main characters. One is never quite sure how LeMerle will manipulate events and if Juliette will continue to be a victim or emerge victorious. She knows LeMerle’s favors always come with a price and the story reaches a turning point when she realizes that pride is all he has.<br /><br />This is the fourth Joanne Harris book I’ve read and I have yet to be disappointed.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10890676567437178764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1888370580" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1888370580" />
    <a title="Natasa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3742075-natasa"><img alt="Natasa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533387613p2/3742075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888370580?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasa" href="/user/show/3742075-natasa">Natasa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888370580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4194344219284305963">The plot of this novel is fairly original, and the beginning seemed promising. Where it failed, was on the actual execution of the plot, and motivation of characters. The whole plot just seems unlikely. Things happen without explanation, and it is hard to believe how these people got from what they used to be to what they are. Another problem is that this book did not give me the feel of the time period. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_392495668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392495668" />
    <a title="Sharon Bolton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6225577-sharon-bolton"><img alt="Sharon Bolton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442481009p2/6225577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392495668?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Bolton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Bolton" href="/user/show/6225577-sharon-bolton">Sharon Bolton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392495668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5942361209648446337">‘Time’s black rosary counts the interminable seconds.’<br/> <br/>In 17th Century France, Soeur Auguste lives a gentle, generous life in the remote island abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-Mer, together with her daughter, Fleur. She is loved and valued by her sisters in faith, as much for her skills with medicinal plants as for her sweet and kindly nature. But Soeur Auguste is hiding a secret. She is not the impoverished widow of her ‘cover story,’ but Juliette, a one-time gypsy and circus performer, forced by t</span>
  <span id="freeText5942361209648446337" style="display:none">‘Time’s black rosary counts the interminable seconds.’<br /> <br />In 17th Century France, Soeur Auguste lives a gentle, generous life in the remote island abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-Mer, together with her daughter, Fleur. She is loved and valued by her sisters in faith, as much for her skills with medicinal plants as for her sweet and kindly nature. But Soeur Auguste is hiding a secret. She is not the impoverished widow of her ‘cover story,’ but Juliette, a one-time gypsy and circus performer, forced by the betrayal of a man she loved to seek refuge in holy orders. <br /><br />For the first five years of Fleur’s life, all goes well, and if Juliette feels at all restless and confined in her new life, the joy she has in her daughter and her friendship with the Abbess and some of the other nuns more than make up for it. <br />But then the old Abbess dies, and her successor is the eleven-year-old daughter of a corrupt and noble family, fanatically bent on reform. Worse still, the new Abbess has brought as her confessor and guiding priest an imposter with an evil agenda of his own. Pere Colombin is none other than Guy LeMerle (the Blackbird) the man who betrayed Juliette five years earlier. To survive in the new order and protect those she cares about, Juliette has no choice but to fight LeMerle in an increasingly dangerous battle of wits that, ultimately, only one of them can survive. <br /> <br />The book starts sweetly, if a little slowly, as we alternate between Juliette’s life in the abbey and her recollections of an earlier time on the road. It was no charmed existence: she was orphaned, separated from her adopted family, driven to begging and prostitution to survive, used selfishly by the man she loved and finally abandoned to an almost certain death. And yet, Harris captures the rich, heady essence of 17th century gypsy life in the way that, to my mind, Stef Penney completely failed to do for its 20th century equivalent in The Invisible Ones. Harris paints a wonderful, colourful picture; not a pretty one, by any means, but one completely compelling. <br /><br />What might be disappointing for Harris fans is that the character of Juliette can seem rather too similar to that of Vianne Rocher (Chocolat, The Lollipop Shoes and Peaches for Monsieur Le Cure) and to some extent that of Framboise (Five Quarters of The Orange. There was a sense, in the Juliette-narrated chapters, of going over old ground but the book comes to life gloriously with the entrance of Guy LeMerle, a fascinatingly immoral creation, who values others only in that they can be of use to him or amuse him and who remains irrepressible and unrepentant till the end. <br /><br />The follies of organized religion are themes that Harris refers to frequently in her work, but in no other book is the danger of denying natural human impulses more thoroughly explored than in this. The convent seethes with the stench of repressed sexuality and resonates with the frustrations of lives left unsatisfied. The abbey is like dry kindling in the hot sun. One spark and everything is set to erupt. <br /><br />Harris shows the freefall into disorder perfectly. The simple country nuns soon become confused, attention seeking, spiteful and, ultimately, hysterical under the twin influences of LeMerle’s mischief and the Abbess’s misplaced zeal. We can only watch with dismay. <br /><br />The Holy Fools is probably not the best of Harris’s books, but given that her “worst” would still be streets ahead of the best of most other writers, it’s well worth a read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5942361209648446337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14257024?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy" href="/user/show/82490-stacy">Stacy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060559137" href="/book/show/15146.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">French gypsies from the Renaissance</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacy by: </span>
      Erin
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14257024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1590879411566853845">One of the reasons I like to read historical fiction set in far away places is I learn about history and far away places. This book doesn't give that satisfaction because instead of doing historical and locational research, the author made stuff up. She sets much of the action in a nunnery on an island near the southern town Saintes-Maries-de-la-Mer. I've actually been to this town, and there's no island and no nunnery there. I think she was inspired by the island monastary of Mont St. Michel, o</span>
  <span id="freeText1590879411566853845" style="display:none">One of the reasons I like to read historical fiction set in far away places is I learn about history and far away places. This book doesn't give that satisfaction because instead of doing historical and locational research, the author made stuff up. She sets much of the action in a nunnery on an island near the southern town Saintes-Maries-de-la-Mer. I've actually been to this town, and there's no island and no nunnery there. I think she was inspired by the island monastary of Mont St. Michel, on the other end of the country, where the monks really are isolated at high tide (or would have been before the modern causeway was built). Also, Juliet's ideas about everything from hygiene to religion are way more 21st century than 17th century.<br /><br />Still... I sped right through this book. Inaccurate, unbelievable, and formulaic. And a fun, relaxing read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1590879411566853845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8343112631071624226">Why oh why did I keep reading this book? I thought it would get better and I got caught up in the characters. I regret the time spent!   <span id="freeText8343112631071624226" style="display:none">Why oh why did I keep reading this book? I thought it would get better and I got caught up in the characters. I regret the time spent! It was interesting yes, the time period of 1610 which I know nothing about. And I got taken in by the mysterious Juliette with her secrets hiding out in an out of the way abbey. <br /><br />I found the writing difficult to follow. The main parts divided into 4 characters. BUT sometimes the narration in those parts was not that character so the reader needed to figure out who was who. (ok maybe it is easier if I hadn't been half asleep while reading). <br /><br />I also absolutely hated the ending. Why or why did the Juliette have to be so stupid??? <br /><br />I did like how the author named the book and brought the title into the story. That was well done. I don't think I'll read this author again. </span>

<div id="review_2477148697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2477148697" />
    <a title="Ilana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59371159-ilana"><img alt="Ilana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563253235p2/59371159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2477148697?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilana" href="/user/show/59371159-ilana">Ilana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9780060586249" href="/book/show/2091842.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=17th-century">17th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=france">france</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2477148697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15882691113088775947">Soeur Auguste, once known for her stage name of "l'Ailée" (The Winged One) has found sanctuary at the Abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-mer since 1605 when she arrived there pregnant and made a home for herself and daughter. The Reverend Mother was a kind and lax woman, and many of the sisters were not of a religious disposition, much like Soeur Auguste herself, which allowed her a comfortable position there, tending the herb garden and making healing potions for the sisters which she has learned how </span>
  <span id="freeText15882691113088775947" style="display:none">Soeur Auguste, once known for her stage name of "l'Ailée" (The Winged One) has found sanctuary at the Abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-mer since 1605 when she arrived there pregnant and made a home for herself and daughter. The Reverend Mother was a kind and lax woman, and many of the sisters were not of a religious disposition, much like Soeur Auguste herself, which allowed her a comfortable position there, tending the herb garden and making healing potions for the sisters which she has learned how to make since her gipsy childhood and from her friendship with an old Jewish sage and alchemist. <br /><br />But now it is five years later, and in 1610 many changes are about, and Soeur Auguste keeps a journal of the daily changes going on at the Abbey. The Reverend Mother at the age of 73—a very elderly woman in the 17th century—has suddenly perished, and soon arrives a twelve-year-old child, the niece to a powerful Bishop, to replace her. At first none of the sisters are willing to believe this child will be their leader, but she quickly makes her position clear: she is intent on bringing many reforms and bringing order and strict religion back to the Abbey. This child, the Abbess Isabelle, is not alone either, accompanying her is her personal confessor and spiritual guide, one ostensibly called Père Colombin. But Soeur Auguste, once called Juliette, knows him by quite another name. She knows him as Guy LeMerle, for he was once her lover, ten years her senior and the leader of a troupe of actors and performers, who abandoned her and the whole troupe in a town in the midst of a great commotion when they were accused of brining the plague to save his own skin. That was the last time she had seen him. Now he is at the Abbey for what can only be a dangerous scheme that only Soeur Auguste can uncover to save herself and her daughter... and the sisters. <br /><br />As I am a fan of Joanne Harris and have previously enjoyed historical fiction set in the middle ages and in convents and abbeys, too, I was pretty much grabbed by this story from the first. There was enough scandal and drama throughout to keep things going at a good clip, but I must say I was disappointed by the ending, which came down to a choice Juliette had to make and which I cannot reveal for obvious reasons. I'm not sure why Harris made that choice as a writer. <i>
  <b>Possible spoiler:</b>
</i> Perhaps to give her Juliette a depth of character that transcends mere logic and feminist agendas. That's enough for me to make my peace with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15882691113088775947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3419707920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3419707920" />
    <a title="ReadsALot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62090459-readsalot"><img alt="ReadsALot" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3419707920?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ReadsALot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ReadsALot" href="/user/show/62090459-readsalot">ReadsALot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62090459-readsalot?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62090459-readsalot?shelf=magic-realism">magic-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3419707920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16720230190783582645">I read and enjoyed Chocolat by Joanne Harris long ago, so my expectations for this book were high.<br/><br/>In Holy Fools, Juliette and her daughter, Fleur, live in a convent where they are hiding from Juliette's turbulent and troubled past, which is related in flashback type sequences by Juliette for the first half of the book. We learn of her relationship with LeMerle, and her own sins of the past, and the reason for her hiding. <br/><br/>It wasn't until the first paragraph of chapter six that the book grabbed me</span>
  <span id="freeText16720230190783582645" style="display:none">I read and enjoyed Chocolat by Joanne Harris long ago, so my expectations for this book were high.<br /><br />In Holy Fools, Juliette and her daughter, Fleur, live in a convent where they are hiding from Juliette's turbulent and troubled past, which is related in flashback type sequences by Juliette for the first half of the book. We learn of her relationship with LeMerle, and her own sins of the past, and the reason for her hiding. <br /><br />It wasn't until the first paragraph of chapter six that the book grabbed me. Before that, I picked it up and put it down a few times (and finished another entire book). Still, I did get hooked. The writing is good, very evocative. Ms Harris made her places and characters come to life. So much so that I stayed up all night to finally finish. Thus the three stars. The story kept me entertained. Mostly. At some point, the narrative changed for the worse. Juliette was no longer the sole narrator. Who's head were we in? Was the narrator of the moment talking or simply thinking? Who knew what? How much time had passed? It started on July 5th and ended on August 14 (before zooming into the following year), yet at some point LeMerle referred to the months that had passed. Is that allowed in magic-realism? <br /><br />The author did a good job of push/pull in making the heroine likable and unlikable in turns, while keeping me in a forgiving frame of mind. The secondary characters were well fleshed out - more good writing. Still, this book was too long by far, but I soldiered on, hoping. The end was sorely disappointing, however. And she left a few too many plot holes for my liking. I'm still confused. <br /><br />That said, magic-realism isn't my first choice. If you are a fan of the genre, give this one a go. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16720230190783582645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106356988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106356988" />
    <a title="Libby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3222446-libby"><img alt="Libby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264802672p2/3222446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106356988?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Libby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Libby" href="/user/show/3222446-libby">Libby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222446-libby?shelf=unforgettable">unforgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222446-libby?shelf=great-historical-fiction">great-historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106356988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5941889273780633349">The isolated convent of Ste. Marie de Mer is an ideal refuge for Juliette, once a gypsy player and the famous acrobat L'Ailee. She has fled to this obscure haven to bear her daughter, Fleur, and to heal from the betrayals of her former life. She most particularly wishes to forget La Merle, the Blackbird, leader of her former troupe, her sometime lover and her betrayer. But all idylls end, and with the death of kind and frail Mere Marie, the elderly abbess, come changes that will profoundly alter</span>
  <span id="freeText5941889273780633349" style="display:none">The isolated convent of Ste. Marie de Mer is an ideal refuge for Juliette, once a gypsy player and the famous acrobat L'Ailee. She has fled to this obscure haven to bear her daughter, Fleur, and to heal from the betrayals of her former life. She most particularly wishes to forget La Merle, the Blackbird, leader of her former troupe, her sometime lover and her betrayer. But all idylls end, and with the death of kind and frail Mere Marie, the elderly abbess, come changes that will profoundly alter the nuns, Juliette and the abbey. The new Abbess, appointed by the Crown, is an aristocratic child, fanatically austere, and credulously dependent on her confessor, Pere Columbin. Juliette is appalled to recognize Pere Columbin as La Merle, who had used her and then abandoned her in the hands of witch hunters. She immediately decides to flee, but discovers she has been forestalled; her beloved daughter has disappeared and she knows La Merle has abducted her. With Fleur in La Merle's hands, Juliette is compelled to cooperate in the Blackbird's schemes until she can devise a counter scheme to free herself, her daughter and her fellow nuns. What follows will fascinate and tantalize even the most sophisticated and jaded readers. This book has it all, from gypsy caravans to glittering courts, to the salt marshes of Brittany, we find sensuous sex, revenge both cold and hot, malice, thwarted love, intrigue, arrogance and maternal tenderness. The author is exceptionally skilled at creating atmosphere: the reader can feel the dankness in the dungeons and smell the salt winds from the sea. I have enjoyed previous novels from this author, but this one just swept me away to 1605, to a France so real that I still seem to feel it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5941889273780633349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1499311558?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette" href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette">Jeanette</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1499311558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12717092098573615808">Well written. Joanne Harris tells a tale again that just flows. Her continuity, despite having depth of copy for different time periods within the same novel is superlative. And the foodie details and location placements are marvelous here, as well. But her Juliette and Fleur in the main? They didn't connect with me as much as they did within the former Harris books I have read. It's still an excellent tale and I'm sure quite possible too.<br/><br/>But I do find that there is a rather revisionist slant to</span>
  <span id="freeText12717092098573615808" style="display:none">Well written. Joanne Harris tells a tale again that just flows. Her continuity, despite having depth of copy for different time periods within the same novel is superlative. And the foodie details and location placements are marvelous here, as well. But her Juliette and Fleur in the main? They didn't connect with me as much as they did within the former Harris books I have read. It's still an excellent tale and I'm sure quite possible too.<br /><br />But I do find that there is a rather revisionist slant to sensibilities here that doesn't sit well within the period of the child King Louie. And not only in the depiction of Catholicism itself either. Abbeys and convents, monasteries- all religious orders "on the road" as well- were certainly a mixed bag. But the sense of amorality so developed that it is named in Sister by herself? <br /><br />Says a whole more about the author than it does for and about the story line, IMHO. The psychological depth of the bad guy or of the under characters motives was not as superbly told as in "Five Quarters of the Orange". That disappointed. But it was a good and well written book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12717092098573615808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText17274184736704133234" style="display:none">So, at least I've come to read Joanne Harris' newest book. It was just as great as the previous ones. What is clear is that JH always writes about the same themes: searching for a home, settling down, running away from the past, relationship to dead mother, mystical elements... an so on. <br /><br />This time the book is set in yet an other time, year 1610, but is still in France of course. The main character is called Juliette, and is a former rope-dancer from a circus. She seeks refuge in a remote Abbey with her little daughter Feur. Everything goes well until Juliette’s ex-lover appears...<br /><br />Even the book might not be JH's best, it is very exiting and never boring. The environment is well described, although JH's special touch is somewhat weaker than in the other books. I would also have liked a better picture of the 1700 century. Well, but it was moving still...</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74914852" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74914852?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385603645" href="/book/show/902747.Holy_Fools">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=historical-fiction-alternatehistory">historical-fiction-alternatehistory</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74914852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12086215697522998456">Easy to read and fun. Joanne Harris' books are always wonderful, though ever since reading Chocolat I tend to think of them like the Belgian chocolates shaped like shells: very sweet, but you can have too much. There are some gorgeous descriptions.<br/><br/>The themes and characters, though, are quite similar to those in Joanne Harris' other work. Juliette shares a lot of characteristics with Vianne; Fleur with Anouk. Juliette's cantrips and her herbs are very reminiscent of Vianne. LeMerle is very like M</span>
  <span id="freeText12086215697522998456" style="display:none">Easy to read and fun. Joanne Harris' books are always wonderful, though ever since reading Chocolat I tend to think of them like the Belgian chocolates shaped like shells: very sweet, but you can have too much. There are some gorgeous descriptions.<br /><br />The themes and characters, though, are quite similar to those in Joanne Harris' other work. Juliette shares a lot of characteristics with Vianne; Fleur with Anouk. Juliette's cantrips and her herbs are very reminiscent of Vianne. LeMerle is very like Mose from Sleep, Pale Sister. Etc. The only book of hers that, to me, stands out as quite different from the others is Runemarks, which is based on a different sort of mythology altogether.<br /><br />I think if I read Joanne Harris' books all at once, the similarities would be too much. As light reading in between other books, though, it's lovely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12086215697522998456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933216028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10796126330586355508">Very disappointing book. Weak plot: young girl becomes infatuated with a rogue; she is forced to seek refuge and ends up in a loosely-run abbey; rogue finds her; she is still infatuated, even though he takes her daughter away...yada, yada, yada. What bothered me the most is that his voice was the same as her's - had trouble discerning who was speaking at any given moment. Characters were singularly unlikable. I characterize this book as a "contract crunch" book, where successful authors are forc</span>
  <span id="freeText10796126330586355508" style="display:none">Very disappointing book. Weak plot: young girl becomes infatuated with a rogue; she is forced to seek refuge and ends up in a loosely-run abbey; rogue finds her; she is still infatuated, even though he takes her daughter away...yada, yada, yada. What bothered me the most is that his voice was the same as her's - had trouble discerning who was speaking at any given moment. Characters were singularly unlikable. I characterize this book as a "contract crunch" book, where successful authors are forced by contract to produce a book a year (or whatever terms). I'm going back to reading first novels - always more well written because the author is intent on making a good debut.</span>

<div id="review_1688849568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688849568" />
    <a title="Patricio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50814558-patricio"><img alt="Patricio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577723153p2/50814558.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688849568?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricio" href="/user/show/50814558-patricio">Patricio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789724135854" href="/book/show/2265743.Na_Corda_Bamba">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50814558-patricio?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688849568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3669052488290922613">I've been a Joanne Harris' reader for years, yet this is one of her books I've pushed off because it didn't seem interesting when I was younger. Perhaps it was better this way, as now I fully enjoyed it whereas a couple of years ago I probably wasn't mature enough to love it as much as I did now.<br/><br/>The first part of <i>Holy Fools</i>, told under Juliette’s point-of-view, was such a strong hook and beginning. For five years she’s been a refugee in the abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-Mer with her daughter to es</span>
  <span id="freeText3669052488290922613" style="display:none">I've been a Joanne Harris' reader for years, yet this is one of her books I've pushed off because it didn't seem interesting when I was younger. Perhaps it was better this way, as now I fully enjoyed it whereas a couple of years ago I probably wasn't mature enough to love it as much as I did now.<br /><br />The first part of <i>Holy Fools</i>, told under Juliette’s point-of-view, was such a strong hook and beginning. For five years she’s been a refugee in the abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-Mer with her daughter to escape the life she had as an actress and rope-dancer.<br />I loved how the first few chapters explained the essential of Juliette’s past perfectly and planted the seed of curiosity that only grew with each page I turned. We get a glimpse of why Juliette reinvented herself as Soeur Auguste, but it's only after the death of the Abbess and the arrival of a new one who brings with her a ghost from Juliette's past –Guy LeMerle- that we get the whole picture.<br />Soon, with the abbey obsessed with omens, witchcraft and demons, she must face her fear of him for her daughter's sake.<br /><br />LeMerle was once someone she deeply admired and loved but whom with time became an antagonist. He, too, had a point-of-view in the story and I couldn’t ask for more! They were two characters with completely different personalities that couldn’t help but attract each other, and their narrative voices were different, strong and enthralling, giving the reader two fascinating perspectives of the troubles that appeared in the abbey, their inner struggles and conflicts with each other with origin in the past, and the anticipation of the climax of LeMerle’s game.<br /><br />Throughout the novel I wasn’t just on Juliette’s side or on his - I was longing for the success of both. I despised Guy for what he had done to her, yet I wanted him to get he wanted when I found out what it truly was. There was this constant battle between them of playing each other’s game to get what they wanted which made the narrative intriguing, unnerving and intense as I couldn’t turn the pages quickly enough, anxious to know what would happen.<br /><br />Set in the 17th century France, I loved the abbey of Sainte Marie-de-la-Mer as setting because it was unusual for this kind of conflict and yet it’s something quite Joanne Harris-ish. Adding the amazing prose, fleshed out characters and a surprising outcome to that, I got Harris’ best novel I’ve read so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3669052488290922613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Alongside "Coastliners" it draws such a wonderful picture of Brittany, it's people, landscape and history, that I, who since 2000 meets such people almost every day, cannot stop smiling, if I am not laughing out loud, when I read about them again (and again and again).<br /><br />A must read for anyone, who wants to go on holidays in Brittany or possibly even settle here!</span>

<div id="review_2627751581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2627751581" />
    <a title="Liz Banks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4905029-liz-banks"><img alt="Liz Banks" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2627751581?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Banks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Banks" href="/user/show/4905029-liz-banks">Liz Banks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2627751581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16762006132528418606">This is sooo good! It is written by the author of Chocolat. This takes place in the early 1600's with most of the action in a convent in France. One of the interesting things about this book is hat there is wonderful characterization, but no character development. The main characters remain true to themselves and we ge to see how that plays out in differing situations. It is a mytry wheere you know who will do it but you don't know how or why. Awesome in every way.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1807738542?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magda" href="/user/show/61398252-magda">Magda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61398252-magda?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1807738542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11629632693777796148">Four years after the first time I read this book I decided to re-read it. I had no idea if I still liked the book or not. Specially since the last book I read by Joanne Harris was not a favorite. Holy Fools remembered me why I loved this author's work. The character's points of views are very distinctive even do the author doesn't actually tells you who's point of view is.<br/><br/>Souer Auguste or Juliette is currently living in Abbey of Saint Marie-Le-Mar with her daughter after running away from her pa</span>
  <span id="freeText11629632693777796148" style="display:none">Four years after the first time I read this book I decided to re-read it. I had no idea if I still liked the book or not. Specially since the last book I read by Joanne Harris was not a favorite. Holy Fools remembered me why I loved this author's work. The character's points of views are very distinctive even do the author doesn't actually tells you who's point of view is.<br /><br />Souer Auguste or Juliette is currently living in Abbey of Saint Marie-Le-Mar with her daughter after running away from her past life as an actress. And all starts with the actors as she says right in the beginning. The actors visiting the abbey and one of them probably recognizing her from when she was 'Ailée, "The Winged One," star performer of a troupe led by LeMerle, before betrayal forced her to change her identity.<br /><br />Everything is going to be turn outside when her peaceful live in the abbey is disturbed by the arrival of the new Mére and Pére Columbin. Why? Well the Pére is non other than LeMerle that has come to the abbey with a plan in mind that Juliette is clueless about his plan for the Abbey and tries to run away but the disappearance of her daughter forces her to stay and watch as his plan is set in motion.<br /><br />I will refrain myself from writing more spoilers from the book from now. Juliette is a very interesting character and very well developed. I loved the writing style and how the author made is sound like we were there. But the character that for me that complete stole the show was the villain, well for me he is not exactly a villain. He is more a anti-hero in my opinion, don't know if it's because I liked him or because we both have a problem with the church. It also helped that the character of the Mére Isabelle was absolutely annoying and detestable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11629632693777796148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
